a query to basically a plain lucene string.\n110: \n111:     >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo')\n112:     'title\\\\\\\\:foo'\n113:     >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo bar')\n114: with the special binding rules of Open Library.\n133: \n134:     In our queries, unlike native solr/lucene, field names are greedy, and\n135:     affect the rest of the query until another field is hit.\n136: \n137:     Here are some examples. The first query is the native solr/lucene\n138:     parsing. The second is the parsing we want.\n139: \n140:     Query : title:foo bar\n141:     Lucene: (title:foo) bar\n142:     OL    : (title:foo bar)\n143: \n144:     Query : title:foo OR bar AND author:blah\n145:     Lucene: (title:foo) OR (bar) AND (author:blah)\n146:     OL    : (title:foo OR bar) AND (author:blah)\n147: \n148:     This requires an annoying amount of manipulation of the default\n149:     Luqum parser, unfortunately.\n150: \n151:     Also, OL queries allow spaces after fields.\n152:     \"\"\"\n153:     tree = parser.parse(query)\n154: \n155:     def find_next_word(item: Item) -> Optional[tuple[Word, Optional[BaseOperation]]]:\n156:         if isinstance(item, Word):\n157:             return item, None\n158:         elif isinstance(item, BaseOperation) and isinstance(item.children[0], Word):\n159:             return item.children[0], item\n160:         else:\n161:             return None\n162: \n163:     for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n164:         if isinstance(node, BaseOperation):\n165:             # {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_013hcfmWHt3iG3GGn9qZXxiS","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n2: Crash course Library of Congress Classification (LCC)\\n3: \\n4: Examples:\\n5:  - HB1951 .R64 1995\\n6:  - DP402.C8 O46 1995\\n7:  - CS879 .R3 1995\\n8:  - NC248.S22 A4 1992\\n9:  - TJ563 .P66 1998\\n10:  - PQ3919.2.M2866 C83 1994\\n11:  - NA2500 .H64 1995\\n12:  - DT423.E26 9th.ed. 2012\\n13:  - PZ73.S758345255 2011\\n14:  - PZ8.3.G276Lo 1971\\n15: \\n16: Has 3 parts:\\n17:  1. The class number: e.g. PQ3919.2 ; should match `[A-Z]{1,3}(\\\\\\\\d{1,4}(\\\\\\\\.\\\\\\\\d+)?)?`\\n18:  2. Cutter number(s): e.g. .M2866 C83\\n19:  3. Specification: Basically everything else, e.g. 2012, 9th.ed. 2012\\n20: \\n21: ### 1. The Class Number\\n22: The class number is what's used to determine the Library of Congress Subject. It has\\n23: a pretty well-defined structure, and should match `[A-Z]{1,3}(\\\\\\\\d{1,4}(\\\\\\\\.\\\\\\\\d+)?)?`\\n24: \\n25: For example:\\n26:  - QH -> Biology\\n27:  - QH426-470 -> Genetics\\n28: \\n29: _Note_: According to [1] (page 36), the first cutter is sometimes considered a part of\\n30: the class number. But this isn't discussed in [2], so it seems like it might not be\\n31: entirely well-defined.\\n32: \\n33: ### 2. Cutter Numbers\\n34: Cutter numbers are a somewhat phonetic hashing of a piece of \\\"extra\\\" information like\\n35: author last name, city, or whatever. Each character maps to a letter range, so for\\n36: example:\\n37:   - Idaho -> I33 -> I[d][a-d]\\n38:   - Campbell -> C36 -> C[a][m-o]\\n39: \\n40: For the full mapping of character to letter ranges, see [1] Appendix B1 (page 355).\\n41: \\n42: Because the number part of a cutter number maps to letters, even the numeral is sorted\\n43: lexicographically, so for example this is the correct sorting:\\n44:     [I2, I23, I3], **not** [I2, I3, I23]\\n45: \\n46: In essence they are sort of sorted as if they were decimal numbers.\\n47: \\n48: ### 3. Specification\\n49: \\n50: These aren't very well defined and could be just about anything. They usually include at\\n51: least the publication year of the edition, but might include edition numbers.\\n52: \\n53: ## Sorting\\n54: \\n55: To get _fully_ sortable LCCs, you likely need to use a multipart scheme (as described in\\n56: [2]). That's not really feasible for our Solr instance (especially since we store info\\n57: at the work level, which likely has multiple LCCs). The added complexity of that\\n58: approach is also not immediately worth it right now (but might be in the future).\\n59: \\n60: As a compromise, we make the class number and the first cutter sortable by making the\\n61: class number fixed-width. For example:\\n62:  - PZ73.S758345255 2011 -> PZ-0073.00000000.S758345255 2011\\n63:  - PZ8.3.G276Lo 1971    -> PZ-0008.30000000.G276Lo 1971\\n64: \\n65: This allows for range queries that could include the first cutter. It sorts incorrectly\\n66: if:\\n67:   - The decimal of the class number is longer than 8 digits (few such cases in OL db)\\n68:   - The sort is determined by information that appears after the first cutter\\n69:   - The first cutter is a \\\"double cutter\\\", e.g. B945.D4B65 199\\n70: \\n71: But it works for subject-related range queries, so we consider it sufficient.\\n72: \\n73: ## Further Reading\\n74: \\n75: - Wagner, Scott etal. \\\"A Comprehensive Approach to Algorithmic Machine Sorting of\\n76:     Library of Congress Call Numbers\\\" (2019) [1]\\n77: - LCTS/CCS-PCC Task Force on  Library of Congress Classification Training. \\\"Fundamentals\\n78:     of Library of Congress Classification\\\" (????) \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n2: Crash course Library of Congress Classification (LCC)\\n3: \\n4: Examples:\\n5:  - HB1951 .R64 1995\\n6:  - DP402.C8 O46 1995\\n7:  - CS879 .R3 1995\\n8:  - NC248.S22 A4 1992\\n9:  - TJ563 .P66 1998\\n10:  - PQ3919.2.M2866 C83 1994\\n11:  - NA2500 .H64 1995\\n12:  - DT423.E26 9th.ed. 2012\\n13:  - PZ73.S758345255 2011\\n14:  - PZ8.3.G276Lo 1971\\n15: \\n16: Has 3 parts:\\n17:  1. The class number: e.g. PQ3919.2 ; should match `[A-Z]{1,3}(\\\\\\\\d{1,4}(\\\\\\\\.\\\\\\\\d+)?)?`\\n18:  2. Cutter number(s): e.g. .M2866 C83\\n19:  3. Specification: Basically everything else, e.g. 2012, 9th.ed. 2012\\n20: \\n21: ### 1. The Class Number\\n22: The class number is what's used to determine the Library of Congress Subject. It has\\n23: a pretty well-defined structure, and should match `[A-Z]{1,3}(\\\\\\\\d{1,4}(\\\\\\\\.\\\\\\\\d+)?)?`\\n24: \\n25: For example:\\n26:  - QH -> Biology\\n27:  - QH426-470 -> Genetics\\n28: \\n29: _Note_: According to [1] (page 36), the first cutter is sometimes considered a part of\\n30: the class number. But this isn't discussed in [2], so it seems like it might not be\\n31: entirely well-defined.\\n32: \\n33: ### 2. Cutter Numbers\\n34: Cutter numbers are a somewhat phonetic hashing of a piece of \\\"extra\\\" information like\\n35: author last name, city, or whatever. Each character maps to a letter range, so for\\n36: example:\\n37:   - Idaho -> I33 -> I[d][a-d]\\n38:   - Campbell -> C36 -> C[a][m-o]\\n39: \\n40: For the full mapping of character to letter ranges, see [1] Appendix B1 (page 355).\\n41: \\n42: Because the number part of a cutter number maps to letters, even the numeral is sorted\\n43: lexicographically, so for example this is the correct sorting:\\n44:     [I2, I23, I3], **not** [I2, I3, I23]\\n45: \\n46: In essence they are sort of sorted as if they were decimal numbers.\\n47: \\n48: ### 3. Specification\\n49: \\n50: These aren't very well defined and could be just about anything. They usually include at\\n51: least the publication year of the edition, but might include edition numbers.\\n52: \\n53: ## Sorting\\n54: \\n55: To get _fully_ sortable LCCs, you likely need to use a multipart scheme (as described in\\n56: [2]). That's not really feasible for our Solr instance (especially since we store info\\n57: at the work level, which likely has multiple LCCs). The added complexity of that\\n58: approach is also not immediately worth it right now (but might be in the future).\\n59: \\n60: As a compromise, we make the class number and the first cutter sortable by making the\\n61: class number fixed-width. For example:\\n62:  - PZ73.S758345255 2011 -> PZ-0073.00000000.S758345255 2011\\n63:  - PZ8.3.G276Lo 1971    -> PZ-0008.30000000.G276Lo 1971\\n64: \\n65: This allows for range queries that could include the first cutter. It sorts incorrectly\\n66: if:\\n67:   - The decimal of the class number is longer than 8 digits (few such cases in OL db)\\n68:   - The sort is determined by information that appears after the first cutter\\n69:   - The first cutter is a \\\"double cutter\\\", e.g. B945.D4B65 199\\n70: \\n71: But it works for subject-related range queries, so we consider it sufficient.\\n72: \\n73: ## Further Reading\\n74: \\n75: - Wagner, Scott etal. \\\"A Comprehensive Approach to Algorithmic Machine Sorting of\\n76:     Library of Congress Call Numbers\\\" (2019) [1]\\n77: - LCTS/CCS-PCC Task Force on  Library of Congress Classification Training. \\\"Fundamentals\\n78:     of Library of Congress Classification\\\" (????) Specification: Basically everything else, e.g. 2012, 9th.ed. 2012\n20: \n21: ### 1. The Class Number\n22: The class number is what's used to determine the Library of Congress Subject. It has\n23: a pretty well-defined structure, and should match `[A-Z]{1,3}(\\\\d{1,4}(\\\\.\\\\d+)?)?`\n24: \n25: For example:\n26:  - QH -> Biology\n27:  - QH426-470 -> Genetics\n28: \n29: _Note_: According to [1] (page 36), the first cutter is sometimes considered a part of\n30: the class number. But this isn't discussed in [2], so it seems like it might not be\n31: entirely well-defined.\n32: \n33: ### 2. Cutter Numbers\n34: Cutter numbers are a somewhat phonetic hashing of a piece of \"extra\" information like\n35: author last name, city, or whatever. Each character maps to a letter range, so for\n36: example:\n37:   - Idaho -> I33 -> I[d][a-d]\n38:   - Campbell -> C36 -> C[a][m-o]\n39: \n40: For the full mapping of character to letter ranges, see [1] Appendix B1 (page 355).\n41: \n42: Because the number part of a cutter number maps to letters, even the numeral is sorted\n43: lexicographically, so for example this is the correct sorting:\n44:     [I2, I23, I3], **not** [I2, I3, I23]\n45: \n46: In essence they are sort of sorted as if they were decimal numbers.\n47: \n48: ### 3. They usually include at\n51: least the publication year of the edition, but might include edition numbers.\n52: \n53: ## Sorting\n54: \n55: To get _fully_ sortable LCCs, you likely need to use a multipart scheme (as described in\n56: [2]). That's not really feasible for our Solr instance (especially since we store info\n57: at the work level, which likely has multiple LCCs). The added complexity of that\n58: approach is also not immediately worth it right now (but might be in the future).\n59: \n60: As a compromise, we make the class number and the first cutter sortable by making the\n61: class number fixed-width. (blah OR author:bar)\n                        # We want         : (title:foo ? blah) OR (author:bar)\n                        node.op = parent_op.op\n                        node.children += (*parent_op.children[1:],)\n                    to_rem.append(child)\n                else:\n                    last_sf = None\n            if len(to_rem) == len(node.children) - 1:\n                # We only have the searchfield left!\n                if parents:\n                    # Move the head to the next element\n                    last_sf.head = node.head\n                    parents[-1].children = tuple(\n                        child if child is not node else last_sf\n                        for child in parents[-1].children\n                    )\n                else:\n                    tree = last_sf\n                    break\n            else:\n                node.children = tuple(\n                    child for child in node.children if child not in to_rem\n                )\n\n    # Remove spaces before field names\n    for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n        if isinstance(node, SearchField):\n            node.expr.head = ''\n\n    return tree\n\n\ndef query_dict_to_str(\n    escaped: dict | None = None,\n    unescaped: dict | None = None,\n    op: Literal['AND', 'OR', ''] = '',\n) -> str:\n    \"\"\"\n    Converts a query dict to a search query.\n\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo'})\n    'title:(foo)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo bar', 'author': 'bar'})\n    'title:(foo bar)  author:(bar)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo bar', 'author': 'bar'}, op='OR')\n    'title:(foo bar) OR author:(bar)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo ? to escape'})\n    'title:(foo \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\? to escape)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'YES AND'})\n    'title:(YES and)'\n    \"\"\"\n    result = ''\n    if escaped:\n        result += f' {op} '.join(\n            f'{k}:({fully_escape_query(v)})' for k, v in escaped.items()\n        )\n    if unescaped:\n        if result:\n            result += f' {op} '\n        result += f' {op} '.join(f'{k}:{v}' for k, v in unescaped.items())\n    return result\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

    params.append(('workQuery', str(work_q_tree)))\n\n        # This full work query uses solr-specific syntax to add extra parameters\n        # to the way the search is processed. We wouldn't be able to do our\n        # complicated parent/child queries with defType!\n\n        full_work_query = '({{!edismax q.op=\"AND\" qf=\"{qf}\" bf=\"{bf}\" v={v}}})'.format(\n            # qf: the fields to query un-prefixed parts of the query.\n            # e.g. 'harry potter' becomes\n            # 'text:(harry potter) OR alternative_title:(harry potter)^20 OR ...'\n            qf='text alternative_title^20 author_name^20',\n            # bf (boost factor): boost results based on the value of this\n            # field. I.e. results with more editions get boosted, upto a\n            # max of 100, after which we don't see it as good signal of\n            # quality.\n            bf='min(100,edition_count)',\n            # v: the query to process with the edismax query parser. But this isn't discussed in [2], so it seems like it might not be\nentirely well-defined.\n\n### 2. Cutter Numbers\nCutter numbers are a somewhat phonetic hashing of a piece of \"extra\" information like\nauthor last name, city, or whatever. Each character maps to a letter range, so for\nexample:\n  - Idaho -> I33 -> I[d][a-d]\n  - Campbell -> C36 -> C[a][m-o]\n\nFor the full mapping of character to letter ranges, see [1] Appendix B1 (page 355).\n\nBecause the number part of a cutter number maps to letters, even the numeral is sorted\nlexicographically, so for example this is the correct sorting:\n    [I2, I23, I3], **not** [I2, I3, I23]\n\nIn essence they are sort of sorted as if they were decimal numbers.\n\n### 3. Specification\n\nThese aren't very well defined and could be just about anything. They usually include at\nleast the publication year of the edition, but might include edition numbers.\n\n## Sorting\n\nTo get _fully_ sortable LCCs, you likely need to use a multipart scheme (as described in\n[2]). That's not really feasible for our Solr instance (especially since we store info\nat the work level, which likely has multiple LCCs). The added complexity of that\napproach is also not immediately worth it right now (but might be in the future).\n\nAs a compromise, we make the class number and the first cutter sortable by making the\nclass number fixed-width. If the tree\n    ends up being empty, errors.\n\n    :param child: Node to remove\n    :param parents: Path of parent nodes leading from the root of the tree\n    \"\"\"\n    parent = parents[-1] if parents else None\n    if parent is None:\n        # We cannot remove the element if it is the root of the tree\n        raise EmptyTreeError()\n    elif isinstance(parent, (BaseOperation, Group, Unary)):\n        new_children = tuple(c for c in parent.children if c != child)\n        if not new_children:\n            # If we have deleted all the children, we need to delete the parent\n            # as well. tracking parents\n    \"\"\"\n    parents = _parents or []\n    yield item, parents\n    new_parents = [*parents, item]\n    for child in item.children:\n        yield from luqum_traverse(child, native solr/lucene, field names are greedy, and\n    affect the rest of the query until another field is hit.\n\n    Here are some examples. The first query is the native solr/lucene\n    parsing. The second is the parsing we want.\n\n    Query : title:foo bar\n    Lucene: (title:foo) bar\n    OL    : (title:foo bar)\n\n    Query : title:foo OR bar AND author:blah\n    Lucene: (title:foo) OR (bar) AND (author:blah)\n    OL    : (title:foo OR bar) AND (author:blah)\n\n    This requires an annoying amount of manipulation of the default\n    Luqum parser, unfortunately.\n\n    Also, OL queries allow spaces after fields.\n    \"\"\"\n    tree = parser.parse(query)\n\n    def find_next_word(item: Item) -> Optional[tuple[Word, Optional[BaseOperation]]]:\n        if isinstance(item, Word):\n            return item, None\n        elif isinstance(item, BaseOperation) and isinstance(item.children[0], Word):\n            return item.children[0], item\n        else:\n            return None\n\n    for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n        if isinstance(node, BaseOperation):\n            # (blah OR author:bar)\n                        # We want         : (title:foo ? blah) OR (author:bar)\n                        node.op = parent_op.op\n                        node.children += (*parent_op.children[1:],)\n                    to_rem.append(child)\n                else:\n                    last_sf = None\n            if len(to_rem) == len(node.children) - 1:\n                # We only have the searchfield left!\n                if parents:\n                    # Move the head to the next element\n                    last_sf.head = node.head\n                    parents[-1].children = tuple(\n                        child if child is not node else last_sf\n                        for child in parents[-1].children\n                    )\n                else:\n                    tree = last_sf\n                    break\n            else:\n                node.children = tuple(\n                    child for child in node.children if child not in to_rem\n                )\n\n    # Remove spaces before field names\n    for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n        if isinstance(node, SearchField):\n            node.expr.head = ''\n\n    return tree\n\n\ndef query_dict_to_str(\n    escaped: dict | None = None,\n    unescaped: dict | None = None,\n    op: Literal['AND', 'OR', ''] = '',\n) -> str:\n    \"\"\"\n    Converts a query dict to a search query.\n\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo'})\n    'title:(foo)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo bar', 'author': 'bar'})\n    'title:(foo bar)  author:(bar)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo bar', 'author': 'bar'}, op='OR')\n    'title:(foo bar) OR author:(bar)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo ? to escape'})\n    'title:(foo \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\? to escape)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'YES AND'})\n    'title:(YES and)'\n    \"\"\"\n    result = ''\n    if escaped:\n        result += f' {op} '.join(\n            f'{k}:({fully_escape_query(v)})' for k, v in escaped.items()\n        )\n    if unescaped:\n        if result:\n            result += f' {op} '\n        result += f' {op} '.join(f'{k}:{v}' for k, v in unescaped.items())\n    return result\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":121,"oldLines":7,"newStart":121,"newLines":7,"lines":["     \"\"\"","     escaped = query","     # Escape special characters","-    escaped = re.sub(r'[\\[\\](){}:\"\\-+?~^/\\\\,]', r'\\\\\\\\\\g<0>', escaped)","+    escaped = re.sub(r'[\\[\\](){}:\"\\-+?~^/\\\\,]', r'\\\\\\g<0>', escaped)","     # Remove boolean operators by making them lowercase","     escaped = re.sub(r'AND|OR|NOT', lambda _1: _1.group(0).lower(), escaped)","     return escaped"]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

solr/lucene, field names are greedy, and\n    affect the rest of the query until another field is hit.\n\n    Here are some examples. The first query is the native solr/lucene\n    parsing. The second is the parsing we want.\n\n    Query : title:foo bar\n    Lucene: (title:foo) bar\n    OL    : (title:foo bar)\n\n    Query : title:foo OR bar AND author:blah\n    Lucene: (title:foo) OR (bar) AND (author:blah)\n    OL    : (title:foo OR bar) AND (author:blah)\n\n    This requires an annoying amount of manipulation of the default\n    Luqum parser, unfortunately.\n\n    Also, OL queries allow spaces after fields.\n    \"\"\"\n    tree = parser.parse(query)\n\n    def find_next_word(item: Item) -> Optional[tuple[Word, Optional[BaseOperation]]]:\n        if isinstance(item, Word):\n            return item, None\n        elif isinstance(item, BaseOperation) and isinstance(item.children[0], Word):\n            return item.children[0], item\n        else:\n            return None\n\n    for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n        if isinstance(node, BaseOperation):\n            # If the tree\n    ends up being empty, errors.\n\n    :param child: Node to remove\n    :param parents: Path of parent nodes leading from the root of the tree\n    \"\"\"\n    parent = parents[-1] if parents else None\n    if parent is None:\n        # We cannot remove the element if it is the root of the tree\n        raise EmptyTreeError()\n    elif isinstance(parent, (BaseOperation, Group, Unary)):\n        new_children = tuple(c for c in parent.children if c != child)\n        if not new_children:\n            # If we have deleted all the children, we need to delete the parent\n            # as well. tracking parents\n    \"\"\"\n    parents = _parents or []\n    yield item, parents\n    new_parents = [*parents, item]\n    for child in item.children:\n        yield from luqum_traverse(child, foo\" -> \"title:foo\"\n    escaped_query = str(tree)\n    offset = 0\n    for sf, _ in luqum_traverse(tree):\n        if isinstance(sf, SearchField) and not is_valid_field(\n            sf.name.lower() if lower else sf.name\n        ):\n            field = sf.name + r'\\:'\n            if hasattr(sf, 'head'):\n                # head and tail are used for whitespace between fields;\n                # copy it along to the write space to avoid things smashing\n                # together\n                field = sf.head + field\n\n            # We will be moving left to right, so we \"\"\"\n    Try to convert a query to basically a plain lucene string.\n\n    >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo')\n    'title\\\\:foo'\n    >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo bar')\n    'title\\\\:foo bar'\n    >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo (bar baz:boo)')\n    'title\\\\:foo \\\\(bar baz\\\\:boo\\\\)'\n    >>> fully_escape_query('x:[A TO Z}')\n    'x\\\\:[A TO Z}'\n    >>> fully_escape_query('foo AND bar')\n    'foo and bar'\n    \"\"\"\n    escaped = query\n    # Escape special characters\n    escaped = re.sub(r'[\\[\\](){}:\"\\-+?~^/\\\\,]', r'\\\\\\g<0>', escaped)\n    # Remove boolean operators by making them lowercase\n    escaped = re.sub(r'AND|OR|NOT', lambda _1: _1.group(0).lower(), escaped)\n    return escaped\n\n\ndef luqum_parser(query: str) -> Item:\n    \"\"\"\n    Parses a lucene-like query, with the special binding rules of Open Library.\n\n    In our queries, unlike native solr/lucene, field names are greedy, and\n    affect the rest of the query until another field is hit.\n\n    Here are some examples. The first query is the native solr/lucene\n    parsing. The second is the parsing we want.\n\n    Query : title:foo bar\n    Lucene: (title:foo) bar\n    OL    : (title:foo bar)\n\n    Query : title:foo OR bar AND author:blah\n    Lucene: (title:foo) OR (bar) AND (author:blah)\n    OL    : (title:foo OR bar) AND (author:blah)\n\n    This requires an annoying amount of manipulation of the default\n    Luqum parser, unfortunately.\n\n    Also, OL queries allow spaces after fields.\n    \"\"\"\n    tree = parser.parse(query)\n\n    def find_next_word(item: Item) -> Optional[tuple[Word, Optional[BaseOperation]]]:\n        if isinstance(item, Word):\n            return item, None\n        elif isinstance(item, BaseOperation) and isinstance(item.children[0], Word):\n            return item.children[0], item\n        else:\n            return None\n\n    for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n        if isinstance(node, BaseOperation):\n            # if any of the children are SearchField followed by one or more words,\n            # we bundle them together\n            last_sf: SearchField = None\n            to_rem = []\n            for child in node.children:\n                if isinstance(child, SearchField) and isinstance(child.expr, Word):\n                    last_sf = child\n                elif last_sf and (next_word := find_next_word(child)):\n                    word, parent_op = next_word\n                    # Add it over\n                    if not isinstance(last_sf.expr, Group):\n                        last_sf.expr = Group(type(node)(last_sf.expr, word))\n                        last_sf.expr.tail = word.tail\n                        word.tail = ''\n                    else:\n                        last_sf.expr.expr.children[-1].tail = last_sf.expr.tail\n                        last_sf.expr.expr.children += (word,)\n                        last_sf.expr.tail = word.tail\n                        word.tail = ''\n                    if parent_op:\n                        # A query like: 'title:foo blah OR author:bar\n                        # Lucene parses as: (title:foo) ? (blah OR author:bar)\n                        # We want         : (title:foo ? blah) OR (author:bar)\n                        node.op = parent_op.op\n                        node.children += (*parent_op.children[1:],)\n                    to_rem.append(child)\n                else:\n                    last_sf = None\n            if len(to_rem) == len(node.children) - 1:\n                # We only have the searchfield left!\n                if parents:\n                    # Move the head to the next element\n                    last_sf.head = node.head\n                    parents[-1].children = tuple(\n                        child if child is not node else last_sf\n                        for child in parents[-1].children\n                    )\n                else:\n                    tree = last_sf\n                    break\n            else:\n                node.children = tuple(\n                    child for child in node.children if child not in to_rem\n                )\n\n    # Remove spaces before field names\n    for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n        if isinstance(node, SearchField):\n            node.expr.head = ''\n\n    return tree\n\n\ndef query_dict_to_str(\n    escaped: dict | None = None,\n    unescaped: dict | None = None,\n    op: Literal['AND', 'OR', ''] = '',\n) -> str:\n    \"\"\"\n    Converts a query dict to a search query.\n\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo'})\n    'title:(foo)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo bar', 'author': 'bar'})\n    'title:(foo bar)  author:(bar)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo bar', 'author': 'bar'}, op='OR')\n    'title:(foo bar) OR author:(bar)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo ? to escape'})\n    'title:(foo \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\? to escape)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'YES AND'})\n    'title:(YES and)'\n    \"\"\"\n    result = ''\n    if escaped:\n        result += f' {op} '.join(\n            f'{k}:({fully_escape_query(v)})' for k, v in escaped.items()\n        )\n    if unescaped:\n        if result:\n            result += f' {op} '\n        result += f' {op} '.join(f'{k}:{v}' for k, v in unescaped.items())\n    return result\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":109,"oldLines":13,"newStart":109,"newLines":13,"lines":["     Try to convert a query to basically a plain lucene string."," ","     >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo')","-    'title\\\\:foo'","+    'title\\\\\\\\:foo'","     >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo bar')","-    'title\\\\:foo bar'","+    'title\\\\\\\\:foo bar'","     >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo (bar baz:boo)')","-    'title\\\\:foo \\\\(bar baz\\\\:boo\\\\)'","+    'title\\\\\\\\:foo \\\\\\\\(bar baz\\\\\\\\:boo\\\\\\\\)'","     >>> fully_escape_query('x:[A TO Z}')","-    'x\\\\:[A TO Z}'","+    'x\\\\\\\\:\\\\\\\\[A TO Z\\\\\\\\}'","     >>> fully_escape_query('foo AND bar')","     'foo and bar'","     \"\"\""]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

If the tree\n    ends up being empty, errors.\n\n    :param child: Node to remove\n    :param parents: Path of parent nodes leading from the root of the tree\n    \"\"\"\n    parent = parents[-1] if parents else None\n    if parent is None:\n        # We cannot remove the element if it is the root of the tree\n        raise EmptyTreeError()\n    elif isinstance(parent, (BaseOperation, Group, Unary)):\n        new_children = tuple(c for c in parent.children if c != child)\n        if not new_children:\n            # If we have deleted all the children, we need to delete the parent\n            # as well. tracking parents\n    \"\"\"\n    parents = _parents or []\n    yield item, parents\n    new_parents = [*parents, item]\n    for child in item.children:\n        yield from luqum_traverse(child, lower=False)\n    'title\\\\\\\\:foo bar baz\\\\\\\\:boo'\n    >>> escape_unknown_fields('hi', {'title'}.__contains__)\n    'hi'\n    >>> escape_unknown_fields('(title:foo) OR (blah:bah)', foo\" -> \"title:foo\"\n    escaped_query = str(tree)\n    offset = 0\n    for sf, _ in luqum_traverse(tree):\n        if isinstance(sf, SearchField) and not is_valid_field(\n            sf.name.lower() if lower else sf.name\n        ):\n            field = sf.name + r'\\:'\n            if hasattr(sf, 'head'):\n                # head and tail are used for whitespace between fields;\n                # copy it along to the write space to avoid things smashing\n                # together\n                field = sf.head + field\n\n            # We will be moving left to right, so we need to adjust the offset\n            # to account for the characters we have already replaced\n            escaped_query = (\n                escaped_query[: sf.pos + offset]\n                + field\n                + escaped_query[sf.pos + len(field) - 1 + offset :]\n            )\n            offset += 1\n    return escaped_query\n\n\ndef fully_escape_query(query: str) -> str:\n    \"\"\"\n    Try to convert a query to basically a plain lucene string.\n\n    >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo')\n    'title\\\\\\\\:foo'\n    >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo bar')\n    'title\\\\\\\\:foo bar'\n    >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo (bar baz:boo)')\n    'title\\\\\\\\:foo \\\\\\\\(bar baz\\\\\\\\:boo\\\\\\\\)'\n    >>> fully_escape_query('x:[A TO Z}')\n    'x\\\\\\\\:\\\\\\\\[A TO Z\\\\\\\\}'\n    >>> fully_escape_query('foo AND bar')\n    'foo and bar'\n    \"\"\"\n    escaped = query\n    # Escape special characters\n    escaped = re.sub(r'[\\[\\](){}:\"\\-+?~^/\\\\,]', r'\\\\\\g<0>', escaped)\n    # Remove boolean operators by making them lowercase\n    escaped = re.sub(r'AND|OR|NOT', lambda _1: _1.group(0).lower(), escaped)\n    return escaped\n\n\ndef luqum_parser(query: str) -> Item:\n    \"\"\"\n    Parses a lucene-like query, with the special binding rules of Open Library.\n\n    In our queries, unlike native solr/lucene, field names are greedy, and\n    affect the rest of the query until another field is hit.\n\n    Here are some examples. The first query is the native solr/lucene\n    parsing. The second is the parsing we want.\n\n    Query : title:foo bar\n    Lucene: (title:foo) bar\n    OL    : (title:foo bar)\n\n    Query : title:foo OR bar AND author:blah\n    Lucene: (title:foo) OR (bar) AND (author:blah)\n    OL    : (title:foo OR bar) AND (author:blah)\n\n    This requires an annoying amount of manipulation of the default\n    Luqum parser, unfortunately.\n\n    Also, OL queries allow spaces after fields.\n    \"\"\"\n    tree = parser.parse(query)\n\n    def find_next_word(item: Item) -> Optional[tuple[Word, Optional[BaseOperation]]]:\n        if isinstance(item, Word):\n            return item, None\n        elif isinstance(item, BaseOperation) and isinstance(item.children[0], Word):\n            return item.children[0], item\n        else:\n            return None\n\n    for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n        if isinstance(node, BaseOperation):\n            # if any of the children are SearchField followed by one or more words,\n            # we bundle them together\n            last_sf: SearchField = None\n            to_rem = []\n            for child in node.children:\n                if isinstance(child, SearchField) and isinstance(child.expr, Word):\n                    last_sf = child\n                elif last_sf and (next_word := find_next_word(child)):\n                    word, parent_op = next_word\n                    # Add it over\n                    if not isinstance(last_sf.expr, Group):\n                        last_sf.expr = Group(type(node)(last_sf.expr, word))\n                        last_sf.expr.tail = word.tail\n                        word.tail = ''\n                    else:\n                        last_sf.expr.expr.children[-1].tail = last_sf.expr.tail\n                        last_sf.expr.expr.children += (word,)\n                        last_sf.expr.tail = word.tail\n                        word.tail = ''\n                    if parent_op:\n                        # A query like: 'title:foo blah OR author:bar\n                        # Lucene parses as: (title:foo) ? (blah OR author:bar)\n                        # We want         : (title:foo ? blah) OR (author:bar)\n                        node.op = parent_op.op\n                        node.children += (*parent_op.children[1:],)\n                    to_rem.append(child)\n                else:\n                    last_sf = None\n            if len(to_rem) == len(node.children) - 1:\n                # We only have the searchfield left!\n                if parents:\n                    # Move the head to the next element\n                    last_sf.head = node.head\n                    parents[-1].children = tuple(\n                        child if child is not node else last_sf\n                        for child in parents[-1].children\n                    )\n                else:\n                    tree = last_sf\n                    break\n            else:\n                node.children = tuple(\n                    child for child in node.children if child not in to_rem\n                )\n\n    # Remove spaces before field names\n    for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n        if isinstance(node, SearchField):\n            node.expr.head = ''\n\n    return tree\n\n\ndef query_dict_to_str(\n    escaped: dict | None = None,\n    unescaped: dict | None = None,\n    op: Literal['AND', 'OR', ''] = '',\n) -> str:\n    \"\"\"\n    Converts a query dict to a search query.\n\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo'})\n    'title:(foo)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo bar', 'author': 'bar'})\n    'title:(foo bar)  author:(bar)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo bar', 'author': 'bar'}, op='OR')\n    'title:(foo bar) OR author:(bar)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo ? to escape'})\n    'title:(foo \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\? to escape)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'YES AND'})\n    'title:(YES and)'\n    \"\"\"\n    result = ''\n    if escaped:\n        result += f' {op} '.join(\n            f'{k}:({fully_escape_query(v)})' for k, v in escaped.items()\n        )\n    if unescaped:\n        if result:\n            result += f' {op} '\n        result += f' {op} '.join(f'{k}:{v}' for k, v in unescaped.items())\n    return result\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":230,"oldLines":7,"newStart":230,"newLines":7,"lines":["     >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo bar', 'author': 'bar'}, op='OR')","     'title:(foo bar) OR author:(bar)'","     >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo ? to escape'})","-    'title:(foo \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\? to escape)'","+    'title:(foo \\\\\\\\? to escape)'","     >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'YES AND'})","     'title:(YES and)'","     \"\"\""]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}
